Jamison Brereton

104 (620)
Destroying Demons, Using Imprecations and Curses. Indra and Soma (1тАУ7, 15, 25), Indra (8, 16, 19тАУ22, 24), Soma (9, 12тАУ13), Agni (10, 14), Gods (11), Pressing Stones (17), Maruts (18), Vasist╠гhaтАЩs Hopes for Himself (23ab), Earth and Midspace (23cd) ╠г
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
25 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 1тАУ6, 18, 21, 23; anuс╣гс╣нubh 25; jagat─л or triс╣гс╣нubh 7
This long and rambling hymn coming at the very end of the VIIth Maс╣Зс╕Нala is obvi ously an addition to the original collection, not only on formal grounds but on those of content. Not a praise hymn, it calls upon a series of gods and other powers to destroy all manner of threats to us, in all manner of creatively bloodthirsty ways. It therefore has more in common with what we might term the тАЬinstrumentalтАЭ hymns of the Atharvaveda than with the R╠еgvedic manner, and it is in fact found in almost identical form as Atharvaveda ┼Ъaunaka VIII.4 and in Atharvaveda Paippal─Бda XVI. The relentless focus on the elimination of evildoers and the changes rung on the methods of destroying them can give an impression of homogeneity, despite the number of different gods called on (mostly Indra and Soma, but with a number of others interspersed: see the Anukramaс╣З─л ascriptions above).
Nonetheless smaller divisions can be discerned within the hymn as a whole. The mood is set by verse 1, with no fewer than eight violent imperatives addressed to Indra and Soma, urging action against the wicked. The first five verses follow the same pattern: an initial vocative ├нndr─Бsom─Б тАЬo Indra and Soma,тАЭ followed by imper
atives addressed to those gods. The sixth verse starts the same, with the vocative, but continues somewhat differently: rather than ordering the gods to unleash their powers in yet another way, the poet expresses the hope that his own thought (and its verbal expression) will envelop the gods like horse-tackle. This prayer-offering and the sacred formulations (br├бhman) that Indra and Soma are urged to quicken in p─Бda d brings the brutal first section to a more benign and R╠еgvedic conclusion. Verse 7 is also addressed to Indra and Soma, also in the vocative, but with the vocative postponed till the beginning of the second half of the verse. This slight change in structure allows this verse to serve as a transition to the next subsection, which continues, in our opinion, through verse 11 and is defined by a ring provided by the preverb pr├бti тАЬagainst, in response to,тАЭ opening 7a and 11c. Though the demands for action continue in this section, they take a more personal turn. In the first section, the gods were simply ordered to destroy evildoers; in this section the target is evildoers who act against us (as the pr├бti signals). These verses all posit an innocent victim (usually 1st person) of the malefactor who is to be destroyed by the gods. Moreover, the avengers are no longer just Indra and Soma in tandem; each verse has a different designated hitter: just Indra in 8, Soma in 9, Agni in 10, and the gods in general in 11. The nature of the offenses has also become more sharply defined, in that the transgressions involve evil or false speech (even the тАЬcheatтАЭ of vss. 10тАУ11 means literally тАЬdesire to deceiveтАЭ). Although evil speech and hostility to sacred speech were already found in verse 2, these linguistic offenses were only some of the condemned activities in the first section; they are the only ones here. In the two next verses (12тАУ13), speech, true and false, is foregrounded, and the punishment of the speaker of falsehood is reassuringly affirmed. But the mood changes abruptly in verse 14: the speaker seems to stand accused of the very offenses he called upon the gods to punish; the innocent 1st persons of verses 7тАУ11 are the objects of AgniтАЩs anger. The aborted conditional clause of 14ab seems to convey the speakerтАЩs distress. In verses 15тАУ16 the speaker swears a dramatic oath concerning the truth of his denial and calls down further destruction on the man who falsely accused him. The accusation is that he is a y─Бtu(dh─Б╠Бna), a тАЬsorcerer.тАЭ The speakerтАЩs ringing assertion of his innocence and his powerful curse against his accuser brings this section of the hymn to a resounding conclusion.
Indeed, we are of the opinion that the rest of the hymn was simply tacked onto what precedes because it concerns sorcerers, using the same word y─Бtu, and simi lar demonic beings. The tone of the remainder (vss. 17тАУ25) is very different, with the theme of true and false speech recessive. The enemies are sorcerers in various animal forms, and the sense of personal menace and of human evildoing is almost entirely absent. Nonetheless, even if we are correct that these nine verses were origi nally independent, the fact that the full hymn was transmitted independently in the R╠еgveda and both recensions of the Atharvaveda would indicate that the join was made early.
The Indian tradition (and many Western commentators, including Geldner) reads Vasiс╣гс╣нhaтАЩs biography into the dramatic middle of the hymn, interpreting the accusation and denial in verses 15тАУ16 as evidence for the hostility between Vasiс╣гс╣нha and Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra found in much later texts. In this interpretation Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra is the accuser, and Vasiс╣гс╣нha the outraged 1st-person speaker. Needless to say, there is absolutely no evidence for this in the hymn itself, and no evidence for the

Vasiс╣гс╣нhaтАУVi┼Ыv─Бmitra feud elsewhere in the R╠еgveda. It is always necessary to be wary about тАЬreading backwardтАЭ into the R╠еgveda and other Vedic texts.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Soma, afflict, destroy the r─Бkс╣гasas; showerers (of benefits) cast down those who delight indarkness; put to flight the stupid (spirits); consume, slay, drive away, utterly extermiante the cannibals.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra and Soma, scorch the demonic force, crush it! Pin down those who grow strong in darkness, you bulls.
Pound aside the unobservant ones, burn them down. Smite, shove,
grind down the voracious.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verse contains a remarkable eight verbs of violence, with three in the last p─Бda alone – all quite different.

Griffith

INDRA and Soma, burn, destroy the demon foe, send downward, O ye Bulls, those who add gloom to gloom.
Annihilate the fools, slay them and burn them up: chase them away from us, pierce the voracious ones.

Verbrennt, versenkt, o Indra-Soma, das Gespenst, o Stiere st├╝rzt, die sich des Dunkels freun, herab; Zerbrecht der Thoren H├дlse, senget nieder sie, zerschlagt, zerstosst, zertretet die gefr├дssigen.

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╕реЛрдореМ рдЕрдШрд╢рдВрд╕рдореН рдЕрдШрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдирд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рд╢рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН рдЕрдШрдореН рдЖрдЧрддреНрдп рд╣рдиреНрддрд╛рд░рдВ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдВ рд╕рдВ рд╕рд╣реИрд╡ ред рдЕрднрд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрд░реНрдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ ред рдЕрднрд┐рднрд╡рддрдореН ред рд╕ рдЪ рддрдкреБрдГ рдпреБрд╡рдпреЛрд╕реНрддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рддрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рдирд┐рд╡ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдиреМ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрдГ рдЪрд░реБрдГ рдЗрд╡ рдпрдпрд╕реНрддреБ ред тАШ рдпрд╕реБ рдкреНрд░рдпрддреНрдиреЗ’ред рдХреЗрд╡рд▓реЛрд╜рдкреНрдпрдпрдорд╛рдЩреНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рдЖрдпрд╕реНрдпрддреБ рдЖрдпрд╛рд╕рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рдЙрдкрдХреНрд╖реАрдпрддрд╛рдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖реЗ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЗрднреНрдпреЛрд╜рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреНрд░реЗ рдХреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рджреЗ рдХреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдВ рдорд╛рдВрд╕ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрд┐рддреНрд░реЗ рдШреЛрд░рдЪрдХреНрд╖рд╕реЗ рдШреЛрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рдп рдкрд░реБрд╖рднрд╛рд╖рд┐рдгреЗ рд╡рд╛ рдХрд┐рдореАрджрд┐рдиреЗ рдХрд┐рдорд┐рджрд╛рдиреАрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдЪрд░рддреЗ рдкрд┐рд╢реБрдирд╛рдп рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рдГ рджреНрд╡реЗрд╖реНрдпрднрд╛рд╡рдореН рдЕрдирд╡рд╛рдпрдореН рдЕрд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╛рдпрдордирд╡рдпрд╡рдВ рдиреИрд░рдиреНрддрд░реНрдпреЗрдг рдпрдерд╛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдзрддреНрддрдВ рджрддреНрддрдореН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Soma, fall upon the destructive (r─Бkс╣гasa) and the performer of unprofitable acts, so that,consumed (by your wrath), he may perish like the offering cast into the fire; retain implacable hatred to the haterof br─Бhmaс╣Зas, the cannibal, the hideous, the vile (r─Бkс╣гasa).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Peformer of unprofitable acts: agha┼Ыaс╣Гsa =malignant; hater of brahmaс╣Зas: brahmadviс╣гe = br─Бhmaс╣Зebhyo asmabhyam dveс╣гс╣нre;

Hideous: ghoracakс╣гase= rude in speech; vile r─Бkс╣гasa: kim─лdine = kim─лd─Бn─лm iti carate, to one who goes saying, What now? Thatis, pi┼Ыun─Бya, a spy, an informer; or cruel, vile

Jamison Brereton

Indra and Soma, like a pot on the fire let your evil heat seethe against the one who speaks evil.
Set forth unrelenting hatred against the hater of the sacred formulation, the eater of raw flesh, the one with a terrible glanceтАФagainst the
worm-eater.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The syntactic function of agh├бm in p─Бda a is ambig. It could be an acc. sg.

masc. parallel to agh├б┼Ыaс╣Гsam, the object of yayastu. So Wh (tr. of AV VIII.4.2) тАЬagainst the evil plotter, the evil тАжтАЭ The p─Бda break following it might support this reading. However, it can also be a neut. sg., modifying t├бpuс╕е and therefore the subject of yayastu, as in the published translation, flg. Geldner, followed also by most subsequent tr.

GeldnerтАЩs cited parallel, VI.62.8, where t├бpur agh├бm belong together, seems decisive here.

See also V.3.7, where agh├бm is used as a weapon against an agh├б┼Ыaс╣Гsa-: ├бdh─л╠Бd agh├бm agh├б┼Ыaс╣Гse dadh─Бta тАЬset evil upon him, the speaker of evil.тАЭ The simile particle iva in the simile car├║r agniv─Б╠Бm╠Рiva is postposed, but such late placement of simile markers is not uncommon in the RV.

The hapax anav─Бy├б- is unclear. Oldenberg approvingly cites BergaigneтАЩs gloss тАШqu’on ne peut d├йtourner par des supplicationsтАЩ, and this interpr. seems to inform most subsequent tr., including mine. But this interpr. should rest on the lexeme now understood to be ├бva тИЪy─Б тАШappeaseтАЩ, and I do not see how the morphology would work. тИЪy─Б has a zero-grade ─л, but no ay- forms – but (an-)av─Бya- can only be broken down into ava+ay-a, containing no elements of тИЪy─Б/─л. AiG fails to treat this form. Renou (EVP XVI.114) tries briefly to get it from ├бva тИЪ─л, but decides that ├бva тИЪi is тАЬsimpler.тАЭ This is certainly the case morphologically, but the semantics are harder: ├бva is not a particularly common preverb with тИЪi and when it appears, the lexeme generally means тАШgo downтАЩ (with тАШdownтАЩ the physical direction), occasionally more generally тАШgo awayтАЩ. Renou cites V.49.5 ├бvaitu ├бbhvam, claiming that the verb there means тАШc├йderтАЩ, thus allowing our form to means тАШqui ne c├иde pasтАЩ. But I do not see a тАШcedeтАЩ sense in that passage, just тАШgo awayтАЩ. This is, in fact, the interpr. found in RIVELEX (I.181), which glosses the stem anav─Бy├б- as тАШnicht weggehendтАЩ – тАШnot going awayтАЩ (metaphorically тАШnicht vergehend, verbleibendтАЩ, 181 n. 1) and analyses as a тАЬVerbales Rektionskompositum/DeteтЖРr>minativkompositumтАЭ an- + av─Бya- тАШweggehendтАЩ (тЖР ├бva + тИЪay1

-). This must be the correct analysis, though I am sorry to abandon the richer semantics of a derivation from ├бva тИЪy─Б. My published translation тАШunrelentingтАЩ can still probably stand, as a strengthened expression of тАШnot going awayтАЩ. (Note in passing that RIVELEX I.394 [s.v. ay1

-] glosses verbal forms of ├бva + this root as тАШherabsteigen; Abbitte leisten тАФ descend; apologizeтАЩ; the second terms of the German and English glosses must result from confusion with ├бva тИЪy─Б / ─л and should be stricken.) The rendering тАШworm-eaterтАЩ for kim─лd├нn- here and in the following vs., as well as in X.87.24, is based on a suggestion of Schindler and Werba recorded in EWA s.v. and also entertained by Scarlatta (41). Note that in X.87.24 it is associated with 139 y─Бtudh─Б╠Бna- тАШsorcererтАЩ, which stem figures prominently later in our hymn as well as in other parts of X.87.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Soma, chastise the malignant (r─Бkс╣гasas), having plural nged them in surrounding andinextricable darkness, so that not one of them may again issue from it; so may your wrathful might be triumphantover them.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Inextricable: bottomless ─Бlambana-rahita

Jamison Brereton

Indra and Soma, spear the evil-doers within their hole out into
darkness that offers nothing to hold onto,
so that no one at all will come up from there again. Let this power of yours, full of battle fury, be for vanquishing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich of this vs. contains 2 locative phrases, vavr├й ant├бr (a) and an─Бrambhaс╣З├й t├бmasi (b). Essentially all tr. are agreed that the two phrases are parallel and refer to the same place – and this is reasonable and probably would be the default reading. This interpr. in turn leads some (see esp. Norman Brown and Oberlies I.473) to take this as a description of Hell, or the RV equivalent thereof. My interpr. is syntactically bolder, and perhaps less well supported, but it arises from my discomfort with equating the enclosed space denoted by vavr├б- (which is several times used of the Vala cave, e.g., IV.1.13, V.31.3) with тАЬungraspable darkness.тАЭ Because these locales seem incompatible, I take vavr├й ant├бr as referring to the place where the evil-doers are hiding / taking refuge, and the action enjoined on Indra and Soma in b is to roust them from this hole and thrust them into a dark void with no handhold, the very opposite of an enclosure. A similar use of vavr├й ant├бr as a place from which creatures are ejected is found in the account of the Vala myth in V.31.3 pr─Б╠Бcodayat sud├║gh─Б vavr├й ant├бr тАЬ(Indra) impelled forth the good milkers (who were) within the cave.тАЭ The action there is of course benign, but the loc. phrase also refers to the original location of the cows, not their destination. I must confess, however, that vs. 17 in our hymn, with the phrase vavr─Б╠Бm╠Рanant─Б╠Бn тАЬholes without endтАЭ into which the villainess is to fall, does give me pause. (On the other hand, vs. 17 is in a portion that was probably a late addition to the hymn; see published introduction.)

Griffith

Indra and Soma, plunge the wicked in the depth, yea, cast them into darkness that hath no support,
So that not one of them may ever thence return: so may your wrathful might prevail and conquer them.

Geldner

Indra und Soma! Sto├Яet die ├Ьbelt├дter in die Grube, in die haltlose Finsternis, auf das auch nicht einer von da wieder herauskomme. Diese eure grimmige Kraft mu├Я zur Bezwingung gen├╝gen.

Grassmann

Die Uebelth├дter, Indra-Soma, st├╝rzt hinab in Finsterniss und in des tiefsten Brunnens Grund, Dass auch nicht einer aus der Tiefe wiederkehrt; das wirke siegend eure ungest├╝me Kraft.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra and Soma, scatter around (your weapons) from the sky, pierce their sides with fiery searchingadamantine (weapons), so that they depart without a sound.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Scorching: ajarebhiс╕е, ageless, undecaying

Jamison Brereton

Indra and Soma, make it roll from heaven. With fire-heated (weapons) that smite like stones,
with unaging (weapons) whose murderous force is searing heat, spear the voracious ones down into a deep place. Let them go to silence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

p├бr┼Ы─Бna- occurs only 3x in the RV (and nowhere else in Skt.), here and in VIII.7.34, VIII.45.41. It has no good etymology (see EWA s.v.). The sense of тАШdeep place, chasmтАЩ is thus entirely dependent on context. Such a meaning is compatible with all three passages; the strongest support for it is VIII.7.34 gir├бya┼Ы cin n├н jihate p├бr┼Ы─Бn─Бso m├бnyam─Бn─Бс╕е тАЬEven the peaks bend down, thinking themselves depths.тАЭ Parallel locatives in VIII.45.41 make it likely that it refers to a place, but not what sort of place it might be: y├бd v─лс╕╖─Б╠Бv indra y├бt sthire, y├бt p├бr┼Ы─Бne p├бr─Бbhс╣Ыtam тАЬWhat is in a firm place, what in a solid place, Indra, what has been borne away (in)to a p├бr┼Ы─Бna ….тАЭ In our passage the n├н тАШdownтАЩ does suggest that the destination is a depth, but I also think that this interpr. has been somewhat uncritically embraced by those with preconceptions about the Vedic hell/underworld.

nisvar├бm тАШin silence, to silenceтАЩ contrasts with svary├а- тАШreverberantтАЩ, used of the weapon in 4c.

Griffith

Indra and Soma, cast ye downward out of heaven your deadly darts of stone burning with fiery flame,
Eternal, scorching darts; plunge the voracious ones within the depth, and let them sink without a sound.

Geldner

Indra und Soma! Schleudert vom Himmel her die Geschosse! Mit den feuergegl├╝hten, wie Stein schlagenden Geschossen, mit den glutbewaffneten, nie altersschwachen Flammen, sto├Яet die Atrin┬┤s in die Versenkung! Lautlos sollen sie dahingehen.

Grassmann

Vom Himmel, Indra-Soma, schleudert nun herab die gluterhitzten Steingeschosse beide ihr, Gesellt der jungen blitzversehnen Schar, verstosst die Fresser in den Abgrund, lasst verstummen sie.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the praise invest you, Indra and Soma, who are mighty, on every side, as a girth (encompasses) ahorse, that praise which I offer to you both with pure devotion; do you, like two kings, accept this my homage.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra and Soma, let this thought here encircle you on all sides, like a girth-band two prizewinning horsesтАФ
the thought that, as ritual offering [/invocation], I impel around you, with wisdom (as the goad). Like lords of men, quicken these sacred
formulations.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As disc. in the published introduction, this vs. closes the first section of the hymn, at least as I understand the structure. 140 The preverb p├бri appears with тИЪhi тАШimpelтАЩ only here in the RV (and, acdg. to Mon Wms., all of Skt.). It seems to have been suggested by the p├бri in p─Бda a, construed with тИЪbh┼л, in the meaning тАШencircleтАЩ. The idiom pari тИЪhi тАШimpel aroundтАЩ does not make much sense, unless the image is of h├│tr─Б- compared to horses made to circle a race track. Renou thinks rather that it reprises p├бri bh┼лtu in a: тАЬlтАЩoffrande que (je ceins) autour (de vous en la) poussantтАЭ – but this seems more trouble than itтАЩs worth: he is forced to supply the crucial verb (je ceins: тАШgird, buckle onтАЩ) while relegating the actual verb stem hinomi to a participial adjunct (тАЬen тАж poussantтАЭ).

h├│tr─Б- is of course completely – and not very interestingly – ambiguous between тАШlibationтАЩ and тАШinvocationтАЩ.

In the last p─Бda Indra and Soma are compared to nс╣Ыp├бt─л. Some interpr. (Brown, Doniger) take this as a ref. to the A┼Ыvins, and it is true that the other three occurences of this dual refer to the A┼Ыvins (VII.67.1, 71.4, X.106.4), as duals often do. However, I think itтАЩs more interesting to assume that the poet is comparing these two great gods to human тАШlords of men = kingsтАЩ, a sly switching of the hierarchy of roles. (Of course he just compared the gods to horses, so being compared to humans may be a step up.) I think Geldner is correct in his interpr. of this simile: the gods should encourage our poetic formulations in the way that human kings do, by providing us with material goods. If nс╣Ыp├бt─л = A┼Ыvins, the simile doesnтАЩt work.

Griffith

Indra and Soma, let this hymn control you both, even as the girth encompasses two vigorous steeds-
The song of praise which I with wisdom offer you: do ye, as Lords of men, animate these my prayers.

Geldner

Indra und Soma! Dieses Lied soll euch rings umfangen wie der Gurt die Streitrosse, das ich euch nach meiner Eingebung als Opfer vorf├╝hre. Ermuntert wie F├╝rsten diese feierlichen Reden!

Grassmann

Euch, Indra-Soma, m├╢ge dies Gebet umfahn, wie rings des Leibes Gurt ein Rossepaar; Den Anruf, den ich um euch lege weisheitsvoll, und diese Bitten segnet wie ein Herrscherpaar.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╕реЛрдореМ рддреБрдЬрдпрджреНрднрд┐рдГ рддреНрд╡рд░рдорд╛рдгреИрдГ рдПрд╡реИрдГ рдЧрдиреНрддреГрднрд┐рд░рд╢реНрд╡реИрдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рд╕реНрдорд░реЗрдерд╛рдореН рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрдореН ред рдЙрдкрд╕рд░реНрдЧрд╡рд╢реЗрди рд╕реНрдорд░рддрд┐рд░рддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдорд░рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдЕрднрд┐рдЧрддреНрдп рдЪ рджреНрд░реБрд╣рдГ рджреНрд░реЛрдЧреНрдзреДрдиреН рднрдЩреНрдЧреБрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдГ рднрдЮреНрдЬрдирдХрд░реНрдорд╡рддрдГ рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдГ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд╛рдиреН рд╣рддрдВ рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕реНрддрдореН ред рд╣реЗ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╛рд╕реЛрдореМ рджреБрд╖реНрдХреГрддреЗ рдкрд╛рдкрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЗ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рд╛рдп рд╕реБрдЧрдВ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдорд╛ рднреВрддреН рдорд╛ рднрд╡рддреБ ред рджреНрд░реБрд╣рд╛ рджреНрд░реЛрд╣реЗрдг рдпреБрдХреНрддрдГ рдпрдГ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдХрджрд╛ рдЪрд┐рддреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рджрд╛рд╕рддрд┐ рдЕрднрд┐рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╕реНрдореИ рджреБрд╖реНрдХреГрдд рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome with rapid steeds, slay the oppressive mischievous r─Бkс╣гasas; let there be no happiness, Indraand Soma, to the malignant, who harasses us with his oppression.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Keep (this) in mind! With your thrusting ways smite the deceits of the demon with his wreckage.
Indra and Soma, let there be no good passage for the evildoer who with his deceit ever shows hostility against us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See published introduction. for the init. pr├бti here echoed by that beginning 11c and forming a ring defining vss. 7-11 as a subsection. Since pr├бti тАШagainstтАЩ is not otherwise found with тИЪsmс╣Ы (or with тИЪ┼Ыuс╣г, see vs. 11), I think the preverb has been stationed at both ends of this section to focus attention on the targeted victim. See disc. in published introduction.

The NP rakс╣г├бso bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvataс╕е is entirely ambiguous between gen./abl. sg.

and acc. pl. It is almost universally taken as acc. pl. here, as parallel obj. to druh├бс╕е тАШdeceitsтАЩ, but I prefer gen. sg. for several reasons. For one thing тАЬdeceits (and) demonsтАЭ is a somewhat off-balance coordination (though certainly not impossible in RVic discourse). More important, the second hemistich defines a single enemy who shows hostility тАЬwith his deceitтАЭ (druh─Б╠Б); it makes sense to identify this single foe as the singular demon of p─Бda b, who owns the deceits mentioned there. In favor of the acc. pl. interpr., in X.76.4 (cited by Geldner, n. 7b; cf. also X.87.23) the same phrase must be acc. pl. obj. of a form of тИЪhan, as here: X.76.4a ├бpa hata rakс╣г├бso bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvataс╕е.

On the other hand, in IX.71.1 (also cited by Geldner) in the two-word sequence druh├│ rakс╣г├бsaс╕е, which we also find here, druh├бс╕е is an acc. pl. (as here), obj. of the verb v├йti, but rakс╣г├бsaс╕е belongs to a different syntagm and is abl. sg., construed with p─Бti тАЬprotects from the demon.тАЭ The point of citing all these parallel passages is to demonstrate that even identical word sequences can function differently syntactically in different contexts: the poets were not locked into a morphological template.

The poss. adj. bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Б-vant- (to bhaс╣Еgur├б- [AiG II.2.487], to тИЪbha├▒j тАШbreakтАЩ; see EWA s.v. BHA├СJ) modifies rakс╣г├бs- 3x and hant├бr- once. I choose to render its possessive morphology by tr. тАШwith his wreckageтАЩ (lit. тАШhaving breakage, wreckageтАЩ), referring to the damage that a demon brings in his train – in contrast to 141 looser and more colorful tr. like BrownтАЩs (reproduced almost verbatim by Doniger): тАЬSlay those who employ demons, who hate us, who would break us to bits,тАЭ where he manages to turn both the root noun druh- and the poss. adj. bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvant- into verbs qualifying rakс╣г├бsaс╕е. Others attenuate the meaning of bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvant- to тАШcrookedтАЩ, and then by easy metaphorical extension тАШtricky, maliciousтАЩ (see GrassmannтАЩs тАШt├╝ckisch, tr├╝gerischтАЩ, also EWAтАЩs тАШtr├╝gerisch, mit krummen WegenтАЩ; Geldner, Lommel, L├╝ders 419 тАШhinterlistigтАЩ). This interpr. is based on the second of BRтАЩs glosses of the base adj. bhaс╣Еgura- 1) zerbrechlich, verg├дnglich, 2) krumm, kraus, gerunzelt; see GrassmannтАЩs reproduction of the 1st word of each in his gloss of (bhaс╣Еgur├б). This base word is not found in Vedic – and bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvant- is found outside the RV only in passages based on RVic passages – though bhaс╣Еgura is fairly widespread in Classical Skt., where it generally means тАШbreakableтАЩ, but occasionally тАШcurvedтАЩ esp. in connection with eyebrows (cf. AiG III.195 in addition to BR s.v.). Since the тАШcurved, crookedтАЩ sense seems to be a late and specialized development, I see no reason to impose it on this RVic word, esp. since I see no clear line from тАШbreakтАЩ to тАШbe crookedтАЩ except in such a specialized application.

Griffith

In your impetuous manner think ye both thereon: destroy these evil beings, slay the treacherous fiends.

English translation:

тАЬMay he who with false calumnies maligns me behaving with a pure heart, may such a speaker offalsehood Indra, cease to be, like water held in the hand.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever bears witness against me with untruthful words, as I behave with guileless mind,
like waters grabbed in a fist, let the speaker of nothing come to
nothing, Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme abh├н тИЪcakс╣г here seems almost a substitute for abh├н тИЪcar тАШconjure againstтАЩ, and note that the object (тАЬmeтАЭ) is qualified by the part. c├бrantam.

Renou notes that this is the only RVic pejorative ex. of well-attested abh├н тИЪcakс╣г, which generally means тАШlook upon, look towards, overseeтАЩ in neutral or positive sense. It is notable that in our passage the action of this visual idiom is accomplished by verbal means (тАЬuntruthful wordsтАЭ ├бnс╣Ыtebhir v├бcobhiс╕е). Renou remarks that it coincides тАЬavec le passage de ┬лvoir┬╗ ├а ┬лdire┬╗тАЭ – without specifying what he means.

Griffith

Whoso accuses me with words of falsehood when I pursue my way with guileless spirit,
May he, the speaker of untruth, be, Indra, like water which the hollowed hand compresses.

Geldner

Wer mich, der ich schlichten Sinnes wandle, mit unwahren Worten beschuldigt, der werde zunichte wie Wasser, das man mit der Hand fa├Яt, der Sprecher von Nichtigem, o Indra.

Grassmann

Wer mich, wenn ich nichts arges denkend wandre, mit l├╝genhaften Zornesworten anf├дhrt; Wie Wasser; das mit hohler Hand gefasst wird, sei nichtig er, der nicht’ges spricht, o Indra.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Soma give to the serpent, or toss upon the lap of Nirс╣Ыti, those who with designing (accusative ations)person cute me, a speaker of sincerely, and those who by spiteful (calumnies) vilify all that is good in me.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thosewho by spiteful calumnies: or, those who with violence vilify me, acting uprightly

Jamison Brereton

Those who distort (my) guileless speech in their (usual) ways, or who spoil an auspicious one according to their wont,
let Soma give them over to the serpent or set them in the lap of
Dissolution.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hapax p─Бka-┼Ыaс╣Гs├б- is taken by some as a bahuvr─лhi (implicitly, Grassmann тАШarglos redendтАЩ; cf. Whitney [AV VIII.4.9] тАЬhim of simple intent,тАЭ Brown тАЬhim of pure and single heart,тАЭ Doniger тАЬthe man of pure heartтАЭ [with ┼Ыaс╣Гsa- = тАШheartтАЩ?!]), but by accent it should be a determinative cmpd, contrasting explicitly with the bahuvr─лhi agh├б-┼Ыaс╣Гsa- тАШhaving evil speechтАЩ with 1st member accent, found in vss. 2 and 4. It is surely my guileless speech that is in question, since I was тАЬacting with guileless mindтАЭ (m─Б p─Б╠Бkena m├бnas─Б c├бrantam) in the immediately preceding vs (8a).

As Renou points out, v├н тИЪhс╣Ы probably refers to distortion of ritual speech.

Since p─Бka-┼Ыaс╣Гs├б- is a thing, not a person, the parallel bhadr├бm in b should also likewise be a thing (so Geldner, Whitney, Lommel, Brown), not, as the published translation (тАЬan auspicious oneтАЭ) has it, a person. I would thus take the form as a neut. acc. sg., not a masc. and slightly emend the published translation to тАЬsomething auspicious.тАЭ This something is probably also connected with ritual performance.

Griffith

Those who destroy, as is their wont, the simple, and with their evil natures barm the righteous,
May Soma give them over to the serpent, or to the lap of Nirrti consign them.

Geldner

Die die schlichte Rede absichtlich verdrehen, oder die das Gute willk├╝rlich schlecht machen, die soll Soma entweder der Schlange preisgeben oder in den Scho├Я des Verderbens bringen.

Grassmann

Wer den, der arglos redet, t├╝ckisch anf├дllt, den gl├╝cklichen besch├дdiget mit Absicht, Den soll der Schlange Soma ├╝berliefern und in den Schooss des Untergangs ihn setzen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay he, Agni, who strives to destroy the essence of our food, of our horse, of our cattle, of our bodies–the adversary, the thief, the robber– go to destruction, and be deprived both of person n and of progeny.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever wishes to cheat us of the essence of food, o Agni, or of our horses, of our cows, of our bodies, let the swindling thief who does the theft go to insignificance. Let him be bent double, along with his life and lineage.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take n├н тАж h─лyat─Бm as belonging to тИЪh─Б тАШchange positionтАЩ; in most passages n├н тИЪh─Б means тАШbend downтАЩ (e.g., VIII.27.2), but here and in VI.52.1, also a curse, I take the passive as тАШbe bent doubleтАЩ. Most tr. are unsatisfyingly generic (тАШperishтАЩ and the like). 142

Griffith

The fiend, O Agni, who designs to injure the essence of our food, kine, steeds, or bodies,
May he, the adversary, thief, and robber, sink to destruction, both himself and offspring.

Geldner

Wer uns den Saft der Speise verderben will, den unserer Rosse, K├╝he oder unserer Leiber, o Agni, der Schelm, der Dieb, der Diebstahl begeht, soll dahin schwinden, er soll mit Leib und Kindern eingehen!

Grassmann

Wer uns die Kraft des Trunks verdirbt, o Agni, der Ross und Rinder und der eignen Leiber, Der fall in Noth, der Feind, der Dieb, der R├дuber, der m├╢g’ verk├╝mmern an sich selbst, an Kindern.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay he be deprived of bodily (existence) and of posterity; may he be cast down below all the threeworlds; may his reputation, Gods, be blighted who seeks our destruction by day or by night.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May he be deprived:or, may he exist after his body and progeny, i.e. continue severed from them

Jamison Brereton

Let him be far in the distance, along with his life and lineage; let him be beneath all three earths.
Let his glory dry up, o godsтАФwhoever wishes to cheat us by day and whoever by night.

Jamison Brereton Notes

See disc. in published introduction. and ad vs. 7 on the use of pr├бti to define this section of the hymn and call attention to the victim. As noted ad vs. 7, pr├бti тИЪ┼Ыuс╣г is found only here.

Griffith

May he be swept away, himself and children: may all the three earths press him down beneath them.
May his fair glory, O ye Gods, be blighted, who in the day or night would fain destroy us.

Geldner

Der soll um Leib und Kinder kommen; er soll unter alle drei Erdr├дume versinken. Sein Ansehen soll verdorren, ihr G├╢tter, wer uns am Tag und wer uns bei Nacht zu sch├дdigen sucht!

Grassmann

Verk├╝mmern m├╢g’ er an sich selbst, an Kindern, tief lieg’ er unter den drei Erden allen; Verschrumpfen m├╢ge dessen Macht, o G├╢tter, der uns bei Tag, bei Nacht zu schaden trachtet.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTo the understanding man there is perfect discrimination, the words of truth and falsehood are mutuallyat variance; of these two, Soma verily cherishes that which is true and right; he destroys the false.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thepreceding verses are considered to be malediction upon the r─Бkс╣гasas by the с╣Ыс╣гi. A legend from theMah─Бbh─Бrata is recounted: king kalmaс╣гap─Бda was transformed into a r─Бkс╣гasa when he devoured the 100sons of Vasiс╣гс╣нha. Thereafter, the r─Бkс╣гasa assumed the shape of the с╣Ыс╣гi and said to him: “I am Vasiс╣гс╣нha, youare the r─Бkс╣гasa”. Vasiс╣гс╣нha replied by repeating this verse declaratory of his discriminating between truth andfalsehood; to the understanding man = to the understanding man truth and falsehood are easily discriminate,their words are mutually at variance

Jamison Brereton

Good discrimination is (easy) for the perceptive man: the two (types of) speech, true and untrue, contend with each other.
Which of the two is true, whichever is straighter, just that Soma aidsтАФ he smites the untrue.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The prim. comp. с╣Ы╠Бj─лyas- here (=AV┼Ъ VIII.4.12; also in AV┼Ъ V.14.12), to с╣Ыj├║- тАШstraightтАЩ, should of course have a full-grade root syllable *r├бj─лyas-, like the superlative r├бjiс╣гс╣нha (RV 7x, = Aves. razi┼бta-). Renou plausibly suggests that it has adopted the root syllable of the base adjective – though why other primary comparatives and superlatives tolerate root ablaut is not addressed. ItтАЩs worth noting that if we were to restore the expected form, it would fix a problematic cadence (yatar├бd *r├бj─лyaс╕е ├Я с╣Ы╠Бj─лyaс╕е), by producing a heavy syllable four syllables from the end. As it is, the cadence is тПС тПС - ├Ч, rather than expected - тПС - ├Ч. I am reluctant to emend, however, since it is not clear how the erroneous zero-grade would have been introduced.

Griffith

The prudent finds it easy to distinguish the true and false: their words oppose each other.
Of these two that which is the true and honest, Soma protects, and brings the false to nothing.

Geldner

F├╝r den kundigen Mann ist das leicht zu unterscheiden: das wahre und das falsche Wort widerstreiten einander. Welches von beiden das Wahre, welches das Richtige ist, das beg├╝nstigt Soma; das Unwahre bek├дmpft er.

Grassmann

Der weise Mann weiss klar zu unterscheiden, wenn wahre Red’ und L├╝ge sich bek├дmpfen; Was wahr ist, was das bessere von beiden, das f├╢rdert Soma, Unwahrheit vertilgt er.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSoma instrumental gates not the wicked; he instrumental gates not the strong man dealing in falsehood; he destroys ther─Бkс╣гasa, he destroys the speaker of untruth; and both remain in the bondage of Indra.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Truly, Soma does not promote the crooked man, nor one who sustains his rule perversely.
He smites demonic force; he smites one who speaks what is untrue.
Both lie in the toils of Indra.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Most interpr. (Geldner, Oberlies [Rel. RV I.441], Renou, Doniger, Wh [AV]), take kс╣гatr├нyam here as masc. personal тАШrulerтАЩ, modified by the part. dh─Бr├бyantam, while I take it as neut. тАШruleтАЩ (as it sometimes is; cf. IV.20.3, V.69.1) and the obj. of the participle. The problem with the standard interpr. is that the part. has nothing to govern, and in fact a number of interpr. supply a second kс╣гatr├нyam (or kс╣гatr├бm; see Renou) to occupy that role. Cf., e.g., Geldner тАЬтАж den Herrscher, der f├дlschlich (die Herrschaft) f├╝hrt.тАЭ However, L├╝ders (419), Lommel, and Brown interpr. as I do.

Griffith

Never doth Soma aid and guide the wicked or him who falsely claims the Warrior’s title.
He slays the fiend and him who speaks untruly: both lie entangled in the noose of Indra.

Wahrlich, der Soma f├╢rdert nicht den Unredlichen, nicht den Herrscher, der f├дlschlich die Herrschaft f├╝hrt. Er bek├дmpft den b├╢sen Geist, bek├дmpft den unwahr Redenden. Beide erliegen in der Schlinge des Indra.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf I am one following false gods, if I approach the gods in vain, then Agni (punishes me). If (we be notsuch, then) why, J─Бtavedas, are you angry with us? Let the utterers of falsehood incur your chastisement.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

If I were a man with false gods, or if I call upon the gods wrongly, o Agni… .
Why are you angry at us, J─Бtavedas? Let those whose speech is deceitful to you attend upon dissolution.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The disjunctive тАЬifтАЭ clauses that occupy the first hemistich are more complicated than they first appear. In the published translation I took the first half, y├бdi v─Бh├бm ├бnс╣Ыtadeva ─Б╠Бsa, as a contrary-to-fact expression тАЬif I were тАжтАЭ The general context speaks in favor of this interpr.: in the 2nd hemistich the speaker asks indignantly why Agni is angry at him, so the implication is that the speaker has not done what would occasion such anger. This assumption presumably accounts for GeldnerтАЩs tr. тАЬals ob тАжтАЭ (fld. by Lommel), which is strenuously disputed by Oldenberg But the grammar makes problems: the indicative perfect ─Б╠Бsa should not express contrary-to-fact modality, but a fact in the past (that may or may not have present relevance). For contrary-to-facts of this sort, the pres. opt. usually serves; cf. VII.44.23 y├бd agne sy─Б╠Бm ah├бс╣Г tv├бс╣Г, tv├бс╣Г v─Б gh─Б sy─Б╠Бah├бm тАЬIf I were you, Agni, or you were me тАжтАЭ Note also that the AV version has an indicative present, ├бsmi (Wh тАЬIf I am one of false gods тАжтАЭ). So we must reckon with the real possibility that тАЬIтАЭ did have false gods, at least in the past, and I would slightly alter the tr. to тАЬIf I was (previously) a man with false gods тАжтАЭ The parallel verb in b is the perfect apy ┼лh├й. In the published translation I take this as presential – and this is quite possible, since the other forms of this pf. are so used (see K├╝mmel 489-90) – but K├╝mmel takes it as preterital, and, given my slight reinterpr. of p─Бda a, this might be best: тАЬif I called upon тАжтАЭ K├╝mmel accepts InslerтАЩs 1996 positing of a root тИЪv─Бh тАШrespectтАЩ separate both from тИЪvah тАШconveyтАЩ and from тИЪ┼лh тАШlaudтАЩ (which latter has a full-gr. root med. pres. ├а them. pres. ├│h(a)-). I am not convinced of the 143 need for this separate root and would simply group the pf. ┼лh├й with the pres. of тИЪ┼лh, despite K├╝mmelтАЩs argument that unless the pf. is clearly distinguished from the pres. by meaning or function, they should not belong to the same root.

What exactly this p─Бda is conveying is not clear. Did the speaker call upon the true gods but in a false (that is, ritually faulty or with false intent or a false heart?) way? Such is the interpr. of most comm. – e.g., Geldner тАЬnur zum ScheinтАЭ – but L├╝ders (420) suggests equating m├│gham and dev─Б╠Бn (тАЬoder wenn ich das Falsche als G├╢tter тАж auffasste …тАЭ), though he also gives the alternate тАЬin falscher Weise.тАЭ And Renou is more radical in his interpr. of the verb: тАЬsi j’ai une compr├йhension (fausse des) dieux.тАЭ Given the appearance of the same adverb m├│gham in 15d, with the sense of false speech, the standard interpr. of the occurrence in this vs. seems the correct one, esp.

as it contrasts nicely with the false or untrue gods in p─Бda a.

The question in d is where to construe te. Geldner (fld. by Scarlatta 469, but with ?) takes it as a quasi-agent: тАЬDie Falschredenden sollen dem Tode durch dich verfallen.тАЭ Given that te is an enclitic and that the verb is not passive, this seems a stronger statement than the text would seem to support. I take te with the drogha- of the cmpd drogha-v─Б╠Бc- тАЬdeceitful to you,тАЭ but I admit that it might rather go with nirс╣Ыth├бm тАЬyour dissolutionтАЭ (so Brown, Doniger тАЬyour destructionтАЭ; sim. L├╝ders) – that is, dissolution stemming from you. Not all tr. render the te: it is absent from LommelтАЩs rendering.

Griffith

As if I worshipped deities of falsehood, or thought vain thoughts about the Gods, O Agni.
Why art thou angry with us, Jatavedas? Destruction fall on those who lie against thee!

Geldner

Als ob ich je falsche G├╢tter gehabt h├дtte, oder als ob ich nur zum Schein die G├╢tter anerkannt h├дtte, Agni-was grollst du uns, Jatavedas? Die Falschredenden sollen dem Tode durch dich verfallen.

Grassmann

Wenn, Agni, ich ein falscher Spieler w├дre, wenn heuchlerisch die G├╢tter ich verehrte; тАУ Doch warum z├╝rnst du uns, o Wesenkenner? die L├╝genredner lass ins Elend st├╝rzen.

Elizarenkova

рдЗрдпрдордкрд┐ рд╢рдкрдерд░реВрдкреИрд╡ ред рдпрджрд┐ рдЕрд╣рдВ рд╡рд╕рд┐рд╖реНрдардГ рдпрд╛рддреБрдзрд╛рдирдГ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐ рдЕрджреНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреЗрд╡ рджрд┐рдиреЗ рдЧреБрд░реАрдп рдореНрд░рд┐рдпреЗрдп ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕реНрдп рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЖрдпреБрдГ рдЬреАрд╡рд┐рддрдВ рдпрджрд┐ рдЕрд╣рдВ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕реЛ рднреВрддреНрд╡рд╛ рддрддрдк рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдирд╕реНрдорд┐ рддрд░реНрд╣реНрдпрдкреНрдпрд╣рдорджреНрдп рдореНрд░рд┐рдпреЗрдпреЗрддреНрдпрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ ред рдЕрдз рдЕрдереИрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдЕрд╣рдВ рд╡рд╕рд┐рд╖реНрдард╕реНрддреНрд╡рдВ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕ рдЗрддрд┐ рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рд╕рдГ рддреНрд╡рдВ рджрд╢рднрд┐рдГ рд╡реАрд░реИрдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реИрдГ ред рдЙрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдореЗрддрддреН ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░реНрдмрдиреНрдзреБрдЬрдиреИрдГ рд╡рд┐ рдпреВрдпрд╛рдГ рд╡рд┐рдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рднрд╡реЗрдГ ред рдпрдГ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕рдГ рдорд╛ рдорд╛рдВ рдореЛрдШрдВ рдореГрд╖реИрд╡ рд╣реЗ рдпрд╛рддреБрдзрд╛рди рд╣реЗ рд░рд╛рдХреНрд╖рд╕ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдмреЛрдзреНрдп рдЖрд╣ рее рее рен рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay I this day die if I am a spirit of ill, or if I have ever injured the life of any ma; may you be deprived(r─Бkс╣гasa) of your ten sons, who have falsely called me by such an appellation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Let me die today if I am a sorcerer, or if I have scorched the lifespan of a man.
And he should be separated from ten (generations of?) heroes, whoever says falsely to me: тАЬyou sorcerer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

I use the standard English rendering of y─Бtudh─Б╠Бna- (with cognates well attested also in Oldenberg and Middle Iranian) as тАШsorcererтАЩ (German Zauberer), without any implications about what practices this figure might engage in. Since in the RV the word is found only in тАЬpopularтАЭ discourse, he presumably doesnтАЩt work his ill through orthodox ritual means.

Griffith

So may I die this day if I have harassed any man’s life or if I be a demon.
Yea, may he lose all his ten sons together who with false tongue hath called me Yatudhana.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Indra slay with his mighty weapon him who calls me the Y─Бtudh─Бna, which I am not, ther─Бkс╣гasa, who says (of himself), I am pure; may he, the vilest of all beings, perish.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who says to me, who am without sorcery, тАЬyou sorcerer,тАЭ or who, (though) a demon, says тАЬI am pure,тАЭ
let Indra smite him with a great weapon of death. Let him fall lowest of all creation.

Griffith

May Indra slay him with a mi weapon, and let the vilest ofghty
all creatures perish,
The fiend who says that he is pure, who calls me a demon though devoid of demon nature.

Geldner

Wer zu mir, der ich kein Zauberer bin, sagt, du Zauberer, oder welcher Dunkelmann sagt: ich bin unschuldig, den soll Indra mit m├дchtiger Waffe erschlagen. Tief unter alle Kreatur soll er sinken!

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the cruel feminine le fiend who, throwing off the concealment of her person n, wanders about at night likean owl, fall headlong down into the unbounded caverns; may the sones that grind the Soma destroy ther─Бkс╣гasas by their noise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

She who goes forth by night like a nightjar [?], concealing her own body by deceit,
she should fall down into holes without end. Let the pressing stones smash the demons with their tramplings.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard rendering of kharg├бl─Б- is тАШowlтАЩ; see, inter alia, Grassmann, EWA, and the various tr. of this vs. But I find this unlikely for several reasons. The тАШowlтАЩ is found as ├║l┼лka- in 22a, so it is already represented in this sequence of vss. But, though one could argue that there are numerous types of owls, which could have different designations, there are other arguments against this identification. For one thing, if the word is onomatopoetic, as EWA suggests, kharg(a) is not a particularly owl-ish sound. I tentatively suggest the nightjar. A number of species of nightjars are found in the proper geographical area. As for behavior and appearance, judging from information aggregated from the internet, nightjars are nocturnal (тАЬgoes forth by nightтАЭ pr├б тАж j├нg─Бti тАж n├бktam), feeding esp. at the twilights; the sexes are similar, and the birds are small and therefore could be considered typically female (hence the fem. kharg├бl─Б-). They stay hidden on the ground by day (тАЬconcealing her own body by deceitтАЭ ├бpa druh─Б╠Бtanv├ас╣Г g┼л╠Бham─Бn─Б): images on the internet show them visually almost indistinguishable from the ground and one YouTube video is entitled тАЬIndian Nightjar – Master of CamouflageтАЭ; acdg. to Wikipedia тАЬDuring the day, the Indian nightjar lies still on the ground, concealed by its plumage; it is then difficult to detect, blending in with the soil.тАЭ Moreover, their cries are much easier to connect with 144 kharg(a) than an owlтАЩs, being described as тАЬa continuous churringтАЭ (the internet provides numerous recordings of various types of nightjars). Note that etymologically the тАЬ-jarтАЭ of nightjar is derived from its churring song – and jar and kharg are reasonably close phonetically. Moreover, their genus name is Caprimulgus тАЬgoat-sucker,тАЭ based on the old belief that the birds suck milk from goats; if a similar belief was also found in India, it might seem to be the habit of a sinister or at least uncanny creature – accounting for its inclusion here among the sorcerers in animal form.

The ability of the soma-pressing stones to smash demons, referred to in d, is also found in the pressing stone hymn X.76.4 ├бpa hata rakс╣г├бso bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvataс╕е тАЬSmash away the demons with their wreckage,тАЭ which incidentally contains one of the three other occurrences of bhaс╣Еgur─Б╠Бvant- in the RV, besides the one in vs. 7 above. The demon-destroying ability of ritual implements, especially the noise made by their clashing, also reminds me of тАЬManuтАЩs Cups,тАЭ whose clattering destroys Asuras. See the various Vedic prose versions of this in my Sacrificed Wife, pp. 21- 26.

Griffith

She too who wanders like an owl at night-time, hiding her body in her guile and malice,
May she fall downward into endless caverns. May press-stones with loud ring destroy the demons.

Geldner

Die Unholdin, die wie eine Eule des Nachts zum Vorschein kommt, sich hinter einer Truggestalt verbergend, die soll in endlose Tiefe sinken! Die Pre├Яsteine sollen mit ihrem Geklapper die Unholde erschlagen.

Grassmann

Die gleich der Eule in der Nacht einherschleicht, mit tr├╝gerischem Sinn den Leib verbergend, Die sinke tief in bodenlose Brunnen, und Steine m├╢gen schmetternd sie erschlagen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬStay, Maruts, among the people, desirous (of protecting them); seize the r─Бkс╣гasas, grind them intopieces; whether you fly about like birds at night, or whether they have offered obstruction to the sacred sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Desirous of protecting them: or, be plural ased (to destroy the r─Бkс╣гasas)

Jamison Brereton

Spread out among the clans, Maruts. Seek, grab, crush together the demonsтАФ
the ones who, having become birds, fly through the nights, or those who have deployed their swindles at the divine ceremony.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I am not entirely certain why it is the Maruts who are tasked with the destruction of these creatures, though it is probably because the demons in question have taken the form of birds and therefore are moving in the midspace, which is the MarutsтАЩ domain. Renou also cites the well-known relationship between the Maruts and the v├н┼Ы- (see vikс╣г├║ here), and these animal demons may be associated with the тАЬfolk.тАЭ The root noun r├нp- is otherwise used of cheats and swindles (cf. also rip├║- тАШcheating, swindlerтАЩ), and I am reluctant to allow a sense тАШdefilementsтАЩ only here – though it is the almost universal solution of other tr. (Wh, Brown, Klein [DGRV II.149: тАЬimpuritiesтАЭ], Lommel тАЬUnsauberes,тАЭ but cf. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬUnredlichkeitтАЭ [dishonesty], which has a moral nuance). Deception and cheating are also characteristic of the animal-demons in this section: see the kharg├бl─Б who conceals her own body тАЬwith deceitтАЭ (druh─Б╠Б) in 17b, the flying dog-sorcerers that want to deceive Indra in 20b, and the oblation-stealers in 21b – so the standard sense of r├нpfits the larger context. However, I do have to acknowledge that the root тИЪrip does mean тАШsmearтАЩ, and so тАШdefilementтАЩ is not out of the question.

It is difficult to avoid taking dev├й here as an adjective тАШdivineтАЩ, modifying adhvar├й тАШceremonyтАЩ, a temptation that all tr. (including me) have succumbed to and that is endorsed by Oldenberg

Griffith

Spread out, ye Maruts, search among the people: seize ye and grind the Raksasas to pieces,
Who fly abroad, transformed to birds, at night-time, or sully and pollute our holy worship.

Geldner

Verteilet euch, ihr Marut, in den Ansiedlungen, suchet, nehmet fest, zerquetschet die Dunkelm├дnner, die in V├╢gel verwandelt des Nachts fliegen, oder die, die bei dem g├╢ttlichen Opfer Unredlichkeiten ver├╝ben.

Grassmann

Vertheilet euch, o Maruts, in den H├дusern; sucht auf, ergreift, zermalmt die b├╢sen Geister, Die V├╢geln gleich hinschwirren durch die N├дchte, und die mit Schmuz bewerfen heil’ges Opfer.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHurl, Indra, your thunderbolt from heaven; sanctify, Maghavan, (the worshipper) sharpened by theSoma; slay with the thunderbolt the r─Бkс╣гasas, on the eas, on the west, on the south, on the north.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Roll the stone forth from heaven, Indra; hone the soma-honed one entirely, bounteous one.
From in front, from behind, from below, from above, strike at the
demons with the mountain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬmountainтАЭ with which Indra smites the demons must be IndraтАЩs v├бjra- тАШmaceтАЩ, identified with a mountain elsewhere, as Renou points out: in VII.22.6, as well as in the curious dvandva indr─Б-parvat─Б (3x, only in voc.: I.122.3, 132.6, III.53.1). See comm. ad locc.

Griffith

Hurl down from heaven thy bolt of stone, O Indra: sharpen it, Maghavan, made keen by Soma.
Forward, behind, and from above and under, smite down the demons with thy rocky weapon.

English translation:

тАЬThey advance, accompanied by dogs; desirous to destroy him, they assail the indomitable Indra;┼Ъakra whets his thunderbolt for the miscreants; quickly let him hurl the bolt upon the fiends.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These very dog-sorcerers are flying. Those inclined to deceit desire to deceive Indra, the undeceivable.
The able one is honing his weapon of death for the slanderers. Now he discharges the missile toward the sorcerers.

Griffith

They fly, the demon dogs, and, bent on mischief, fain would they harm indomitable Indra.
Sakra makes sharp his weapon for the wicked: now, let him cast his bolt at fiendish wizards.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndra has ever been the discomfiter of the evil spirits coming to obstruct (the rites of) the offerers ofoblations; ┼Ъakra advances, crushing the present r─Бkс╣гasas, as a hatchet cuts down (the trees of) a forest, as (amallet smashes) the earthen vessels.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Indra has become the one who pounds aside the sorcerers, the oblation-stealers, those who seek to ambush.
The able one, splitting them like an axe a tree, breaking them like pots, advances against those who are really demons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I have rendered the impf. abhavat in p─Бda a as an immediate past (тАШhas becomeтАЩ), though this is not ordinarily a usage of the impf. But this sense fits the context better than a simple past. 145 Note the echo of par─Б┼Ыar├│ in para┼Ы├║r in c.

As Renou remarks, this is the only negative use of the desid. v├нv─Бsa- (тИЪvan тАШwinтАЩ), usually тАШseek to win, covet, coaxтАЩ. The negative sense must be attributable to the confrontational preverb abh├н.

How to distribute and construe the two similes in cd is the question. I take both similes, para┼Ы├║r y├бth─Б v├бnam тАЬlike an axe a treeтАЭ (c) and p─Б╠Бtreva тАЬlike potsтАЭ (d), with the pres. part. bhind├бn (d) in two slightly different senses, тАШsplittingтАЩ and тАШbreakingтАЩ respectively (sim. Brown, Doniger). This pres. part. is anticipated by the preverb complex abh─л╠Бd that opens the hemistich, looking like an aberrant form of тИЪbhid – a low-level ex. of poetic repair. Others (notably Geldner, Wh, Lommel) take bhind├бn only with the 2nd simile, with the first controlled by eti in d (e.g., Geldner тАЬ┼Ъakra f├дhrt auf die Dunkelm├дnner los wie die Axt in den BaumтАЭ). But axes are more likely to тАЬsplitтАЭ than to тАЬadvance,тАЭ and I take eti only with the acc. pl. (sat├бс╕е тАж) rakс╣г├бsaс╕е as goal. It would also be possible to take bhind├бn + eti as a verb phrase with auxiliary, тАШkeeps splittingтАЩ or the like.

The function, and indeed the morphological identity, of sat├бс╕е is unclear. With Grassmann, I take it as a pres. part. to тИЪas in the acc. pl., modifying rakс╣г├бsaс╕е. In my interpr.

it means тАШreal, really being XтАЩ, though that could extend to тАШreally presentтАЩ. Renou by contrast suggests that itтАЩs an adverb, meaning here тАШtout ├а faitтАЩ, also probably found as 1st cmpd. member in sat├│-mahant- (тАШentirely greatтАЩ VIII.30.1) and sat├│-v─лra- (тАШentirely heroicтАЩ VI.75.9). Although Renou does not pronounce on the morphological analysis, AiG II.1.237 implies that it contains the adverbial ablatival suffix -tas / -t├бs and thus does not belong to the pres. part. of тИЪas. See also EWA s.v. sat├бs. Oldenberg (ad VII.32.24) allows several possibilities, incl. the adverb, which he considers assured in the cmpds. cited above. Although, with Oldenberg, etc., I think that an adverbial sat├бс╕е is found in those cmpds., I do not find that interpr. sat├бс╕е as adverbial here improves the sense, though I grant that the acc. pl. pres. part. doesnтАЩt really either.

Griffith

Indra hath ever been the fiends’ destroyer who spoil oblations of the Gods’ invokers:
Yea, Sakra, like an axe that splits the timber, attacks and smashes them like earthen vessels.

Geldner

Indra ward der Zerschmetterer der b├╢sen Geister, die das Opfer st├╢ren, und die nachstellen. Sakra f├дhrt auf die Dunkelm├дnner los wie die Axt in den Baum, sie gleichm├д├Яig wie T├╢pfe zerbrechend.

Grassmann

Indra war der Vernichter der Zaubergeister und der Opferst├╢rer, die sich wider ihn rotten; der starke greift die, welche des Nachts spuken, an wie ein scharfes Beil den Waldbaum, wie wenn er Trinkbecher zerbr├дche.

Elizarenkova

Destroy him shaped as eagle or as vulture as with a stone, O Indra, crush the demon.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLet not the r─Бkс╣гasas do us harm; let the dawn drive away the pairs of evil spirits exclaiming, “Whatnote is this”; may the earth protect us from terrestrial, the firmament protect us from celestial, wickednesс╣гтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Exclaiming: “What now is this?” kim─лdina

Jamison Brereton

DonтАЩt let the demonic power of the sorcerers reach us. Let (Dawn) banish with her dawning the pair that are worm-eaters.
Let Earth protect us from earthly constraint; let the Midspace protect us from heavenly (constraint).

Jamison Brereton Notes

Acdg. to Renou, Mehendale interpr. the curious formation y─Бtum─Б╠Бvant- in p─Бda a (also I.36.20, VII.1.5, VIII.60.20) not as a metrical variant of y─Бtum├бnt- (so AiG II.2.775) but as a haplology for *y─Бtu-m─Бyy─Б╠Бvant-. I assume (I have not seen the art.) that his posited form contains -m─Бy─Б╠Б- in one form or another and anticipates the next vs. where the female sorcerer is тАЬexulting in her magic powerтАЭ (m─Бy├бy─Б ┼Ы─Б╠Б┼Ыad─Бn─Бm), though I donтАЩt know why the form posited is not just *y─Бtu-m─Бy─Б╠Бvant-, containing attested m─Бy─Б╠Бvant- тАШpossessing m─Бy─БтАЩ (IV.16.9). If we accept this 146 suggestion, or modified suggestion, the tr. could be slightly altered to тАЬthe demonic power of those possessing the magic power of sorcerers.тАЭ The kim─лd├нn- was singular in vs. 2, but a dual matched pair (mithun─Б╠Бy─Б╠Б kim─лd├нn─Б) here. Why the dual is not entirely clear, but the next vs. specifies both male and female sorcerers as IndraтАЩs target, and the mithun├б- here suggests a sexual pairing.

Griffith

Let not the fiend of witchcraft-workers reach us: may Dawn drive off the couples of Kimidins.
Earth keep us safe from earthly woe and trouble: from grief that comes from heaven mid-air preserve us.

Geldner

Nicht soll der Zauberer b├╢ser Geist uns beikommen, die Morgenr├╢te soll das Kimidinpaar wegleuchten. Die Erde soll uns vor irdischem Ungemach sch├╝tzen, der Luftraum uns vor himmlischem sch├╝tzen!

Grassmann

Nicht m├╢ge uns der Zaubrer Wuth erreichen, fort jag’ er die gepaarten Frevelgeister, Vor ird’scher Noth besch├╝tze uns die Erde und vor der himmlischen beh├╝t die Luft uns.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSlay, Indra, the Y─Бtudh─Бna, whether in the form of a man, or of a woman doing mischief by herdeceptions; may those who sport in murder perish dissipated; let them not behold the rising sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Y─Бtudh─Бna =r─Бkс╣гasa

Jamison Brereton

Indra, smash the male sorcerer and the female exulting in her magic power.
Let the no-necks with feckless gods shake to pieces. Let them not look upon the sun as it rises.

Jamison Brereton Notes

v├нgr─лva- тАШwith no / broken neckтАЩ is ambiguous: is it descriptive of a preexisting condition and thus a species, ethnic, or personal slur (in English тАЬno-neckтАЭ is an insult, referring to a burly and stupid thug or goon)? or is it used proleptically here, to indicate what will happen to those who тАЬshake to piecesтАЭ (с╣Ыdantu). IтАЩve taken it as the former, but opinion is divided and either would work in the passage.

m┼л╠Бra-deva- is also contested. Acdg. to EWA (s.v. m┼л╠Бla-), flg. Wack., it is an r-form of *m┼л╠Бla-deva- тАШwhose gods are rootsтАЩ (Wurzelanbeter)(see also Brown).

This excursion into exotic anthropology seems unlikely to me – not the sort of divinity that Vedic people would posit even of their worst and most primitive enemies. Most tr. take it as тАШidol-worshiperтАЩ (e.g., Geldner G├╢tzanbeter), without, however, indicating what the тАШidolтАЩ rests on: тАШrootтАЩ ├а тАШroot as representation of godтАЩ ├а тАШidolтАЩ (not a semantic chain that seems reasonable to me)? Or, more likely to me, based on m┼лr├б- тАШstupid, foolish, dumb (i.e., non-speaking)тАЩ. My own тАШwith feckless godsтАЩ is rests on this association, but is closer to the sense of the original adjective. I do not, however, have an explanation for the accent.

Griffith

Slay the male demon, Indra! slay the female, joying and triumphing in arts of magic.
Let the fools’ gods with bent necks fall and perish, and see no more the Sun when he arises.

Geldner

Indra, erschlag den m├дnnlichen Zauberer und seine Frau, die auf ihr Blendwerk pocht! Mit gebrochenem Genick sollen die G├╢tzenanbeter versinken, nicht sollen sie die Sonne aufgehen sehen.

Grassmann

Den m├дnnlichen Bezaubrer t├╢dt, o Indra, das Weib auch, das mit Zauberei sich br├╝stet; Die G├╢tzen tilge, die mit krummen H├дlsen, nicht m├╢g’ die Sonn’ sie sehen, wenn sie aufgeht.

Elizarenkova
